                                          <div data-reactid="285">
                                            <div data-reactid="286">
                                              The T. House is a separate structure on the grounds of the designer and artisan Lili T. ((URL HIDDEN) Originally a garage - it's now a light infused fabulously airy loft-like guesthouse that's very private and accessible at the same time.
                                            </div>
                                            <!-- react-text: 287 -->                                            <!-- /react-text -->                                            <div data-reactid="288">
                                              Food:
Stater Brothers: 4 miles east on Hwy 62 in 29 Palms
VONS: 12 miles west on Hwy 62 in Yucca Valley

Eating out:
Lunch and dinner at the 29 Palms Inn
Breakfast and lunch: Crossroads in Joshua Tree
Breakfast and lunch: La Copine in Landers (Thursday-Sunday 9-3)
Lunch and dinner: Pappy and Harriet’s in Pioneertown 
  (reservations recommended for dinn(PHONE NUMBER HIDDEN))

Entertainment:
Pappy and Harriet’s - best honky tonk west of the Mississippi
fabulous live acts

Nice stores:
BKB ceramics JT (I’m biased - they carry some of my designs)

Sights:
Joshua Tree National Park - obviously…

Pioneertown
Walk down Mane Street and experience this historic Western set.

Noah Purifoy  Outdoor Museum
Noah S. Purifoy ((PHONE NUMBER HIDDEN)) was an African American visual artist and sculptor, co-founder of the Watts Towers Art Center. In the 80s Purifoy moved his practice out to the Mojave desert. He lived for the last 15 years of his life creating ten acres full of large-scale sculpture on the desert floor. Constructed entirely from junked materials, this otherworldly environment is one of California’s great art historical wonders.

The Integratron
Take a sound bath in this historical structure. It’s a resonant tabernacle and energy machine sited on a powerful geomagnetic vortex in the magical Mojave Desert.

                                              <li data-reactid="560">
                                                <p data-reactid="561">
                                                  The first thing I noticed about this rental was that it did not have a porch, which was the main reason that I wanted to rent it. I even brought a folding chair so I could sit on the porch in the morning and evenings. The picture showed a porch, but no porch. It turns out that this owner has a few rental units here, markets them all with this one picture, but you get whatever is available. Rather deceptive, in my opinion. But wait, there’s more. From the picture and description the unit is a cottage in a resort. It is neither a cottage nor a resort. It is a trailer park, the units are all close to each other, and the unit is a small trailer (I know this because I followed the mice who lived underneath and noticed it was simply a trailer). So you hear the barking dogs in the unit on one side of you, and the couple fighting on the other side. And there are cigarette butts and beer bottle caps strewn about to add to the ambiance. The trailer park is located just down the street from the Marine base, so the stores in the area mostly consist of tatto artists, massage parlors that are obviously not for massages, and liquor stores. During the evenings when I would be sitting outside looking at the stars I had a soundtrack of motorcycles and souped-up pick-up trucks roaring up the highway to the base. It literally sounded like a speedway, and the highway is probably no more than 200 feet from the unit, so noisy does not come close to describing the place. But lets not forget the unit itself. After the screen door fell off the first time I opened it, I sat down on the hard and uncomfortable couch, which was nothing compared to the lumpy and squeeky bed. The blanket looked like it hadn’t been cleaned in years, absolutely filthy. The light in the bedroom buzzes to the point where I couldn’t keep it on. There are closets but no hangers, so bring your own. The heater in the living room also sputters. Don’t try opening the windows, you won’t be able to close them. The toilet runs, good luck getting a water temp in the shower that isn’t too cold or too hot, and the coffee maker leaks, so make sure you don’t leave anything on the counter (it ruined a bunch of my vitamins before I realized). Also, hope that the sputtering heater doesn’t catch on fire, since there is no battery in the one smoke detector and it seemed doubtful that I would have been able to escape out the bedroom window. Lastly, if you are there to visit Joshua Tree, you’d be much better off staying in one of the many motels closer to the western entrance to the park, which are undoubtedly cheaper, certainly at this time of year. This unit is closer to the east entrance,...

If you plan on cooking, you'll need to bring a few basics, like a cutting board, salt &amp; pepper, sugar and any other staples you might need. There's a supermarket and 99 cent store about 15 minutes by car if you forget anything.    The bedrooms were small and clean, and our beds were very cozy at the end of a long day of hiking.    One of the things we enjoyed was the quiet and solitude of the location: not that there's a lot of hustle and bustle in the Mojave, we found the location perfect, as it was only 8 minutes away from Joshua Tree National Park, and 15 from a supermarket. We cooked both breakfast and supper in the cabin, and there was plenty of light and a very efficient heating system (we were there for December break, and it went down to the 30s at night....)    There's also a tv with satellite connection and a small couch, as well as a table and two chairs for eating.    Victoria was very available to answer any question and gave us an extra pot when we needed something larger to cook with.    We had a great time and were sad to leave after 5 days!
                                                </p>
                                                <span data-reactid="1320">
                                                  Robert 
                                                </span>
                                                <span data-reactid="1321">
                                                  2015-12-30T00:00:00Z
                                                </span>
                                              </li>
                                              <li data-reactid="1322">
                                                <p data-reactid="1323">
                                                  We were welcomed warmly fairly late in the evening.  The amenities are VERY basic.  When we arrived there were no coat hangers, no hand towels, not enough cutlery for two people and no cleaning materials.  Veronica, the on-site manager was quick to remedy this and within 2 days we had all the things on the list we had provided of necessary items.  The swimming pool is unheated and thus unusable in March.  The internet connection is very spotty and I spent frustrating time finding out emails I had thought sent were still in my draft folder. I was generously allowed into the office to use my laptop there when I had important business to attend to.  The surrounding area is desert wasteland that has garbage strewn around.  Not very good for kids but it did provide a great area for our 2 dogs to be taken on walks.  The furnished cottage itself is good value for money, well furnished and has heat and air-conditioning and is only 5 minutes away from the drive-in movie theatre and 20 minutes from access to the Joshua Tree National Park reserve which is a wonderful walking/hiking treasure.
                                                </p>
                                                <span data-reactid="1324">
                                                  Brenda
                                                </span>
                                                <span data-reactid="1325">
                                                  2016-03-31T00:00:00Z
                                                </span>
                                              </li>
                                              <li data-reactid="1326">
                                                <p data-reactid="1327">
                                                  Based off the listing and reviews, the accommodations met our expectations. The cottages were quaint and private. Located just a few miles from Joshua Tree National Park, it made for the perfect getaway. The onsite manager, Victoria, was very accommodating and responsive to all our questions (at all hours). The only issue we had during our stay was with the keys. Apparently, they only unlock the front door knob and not the deadbolt and the back door. We weren't advised of this at check-in, so needless to say, we locked ourselves out at 9pm. We contacted Victoria and the problem was resolved with the help of the maintenance crew.   The resort provides basic necessities such as towels (no hand towels were provided as stated in the listing) and linens, but we had to buy hand soap, trash liners and additional toilet paper and paper towels. Also worth noting is that there are only two very thin pillows provided, so it was a good thing we brought our own.   Overall, we were quite pleased with our stay. There was ample parking and local markets nearby. Both Noel and Victoria were readily available with any concerns we had prior to and during our stay.
                                                </p>

                                                  Catherine

Outside there where broken glass, nails and wires. Not a place to go around. Furthermore they wanted me to give my credit card infomations explaining that it was state law. When I refused to due to Airbnb policy they say they didn't need them.     It's cheap and close to Joshua Tree. If that's important it's fine. But do you have kids find something else.
